  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9cbe0549-f4c9-400e-bfde-0dd07c1a9c95'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8323902381154875762">The Captive (The Secret Circle #2), L.J. Smith<br/>Initiated into a coven of young witches, Cassie is intoxicated by her new-found strength - powers as addictive as they are dangerous. She is caught between two rival forces, forced to choose between two impossible actions: should she betray the ones she loves, or confess all and risk expulsion from the circle for ever?<br/><br/>The Secret Circle is a supernatural, young-adult series of books created by L. J. Smith. The narrative follows the character of Cassie</span>
  <span id="freeText8323902381154875762" style="display:none">The Captive (The Secret Circle #2), L.J. Smith<br />Initiated into a coven of young witches, Cassie is intoxicated by her new-found strength - powers as addictive as they are dangerous. She is caught between two rival forces, forced to choose between two impossible actions: should she betray the ones she loves, or confess all and risk expulsion from the circle for ever?<br /><br />The Secret Circle is a supernatural, young-adult series of books created by L. J. Smith. The narrative follows the character of Cassie Blake as she is initiated into a "Circle" of eleven other teenage witches and the danger that ensues when they accidentally unleash a dark force upon their town. Matters are further complicated when Cassie finds herself in a love triangle that threatens to tear the Circle apart.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 20123 میلادی<br />عنوان: اسیر کتاب دوم از سری دایره مخفی؛ نویسنده: لیزا جین (ال.جی.) اسمیت؛<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236890526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16260601070199747623">When I review a book, I usually look at two things, first is if the story is good and second is if the characters are likeable.<br/><br/>1. <b> The story </b><br/><br/>I liked the story very much, the suspense was exciting and as they're coming to reach a conclusion I feel that I wanna find it out with them. Sometimes I can't put the book down because I wanna know what's next. Cassie's inside conflict was kind of ridiculous for me but the issue about the evil spirit was kind of cool.<br/><br/>2. <b> The characters </b><br/><br/>I tried really reall</span>
  <span id="freeText16260601070199747623" style="display:none">When I review a book, I usually look at two things, first is if the story is good and second is if the characters are likeable.<br /><br />1. <b> The story </b><br /><br />I liked the story very much, the suspense was exciting and as they're coming to reach a conclusion I feel that I wanna find it out with them. Sometimes I can't put the book down because I wanna know what's next. Cassie's inside conflict was kind of ridiculous for me but the issue about the evil spirit was kind of cool.<br /><br />2. <b> The characters </b><br /><br />I tried really really hard to like Cassie, sure she's got some good qualities but I thought she was really dumb. I mean, c'mon?! Dont you watch movies? Falling for a blackmail is like the stupidest thing you could ever do. I think "protecting" Diana was just an excuse but in fact she can't take responsibilities for her own actions. She doesn't want Diana to find out because she'll hate her. I also didn't like the fact that she's a jealous, insecure traitor, always comparing herself to Diana. Im sorry, I really tried but she doesn't click to me.<br /><br />Now, we're on to one of my favorite characters.. NICK.. haha! I don't know why, he's so mysterious and quiet but he's always there when he's needed. :D<br /><br /><br /><b>Finally, I really enjoyed reading it. Its definitely better than the first one. </b> </span>

  <span id="freeText17902284103911287843" style="display:none">This book was even better than the first one! We get to know more things about the people who form the circle something i really needed because i couldn't distinguish them in the first book. Twelve characters were a lot for me to handle and i'm really impressed with the author because not only she manages to involve them all in the action but she also made each of them unique.<br /><br />I'm glad Cassie got more stronger in this book both in spirit and in magic, seeing the main character being weak all the time in the first book was not so fun. What's also exciting is the fact that Cassie develops a darker side which made her a more interesting character. Then ending too was so intense, i can't wait to read the third book!<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349997239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2916708401617635628">Review at <a href='http://missbookreviews.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Miss Book Reviews</a>.<br/>--<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374832i/729127.png' alt='' width='315' height='60' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>
  <strong>*WARNING: This section contains spoilers for the first book!*</strong>
<br/><br/>Now that Cassie is officially in 'The Club' and now known as one of the 'in' group at school she finds life so much better, she feels welcome and wanted, not like a disease everyone is trying to avoid. Unfortunately for her she is dealing with her desires for Adam, Diana's boyfriend, whom she fell in love with on the beach last summer (One meeting is all it took...). She loves Diana and she would never</span>
  <span id="freeText2916708401617635628" style="display:none">Review at <a href="http://missbookreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Book Reviews</a>.<br>--<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374832i/729127.png" alt="" width="315" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>
  <strong>*WARNING: This section contains spoilers for the first book!*</strong>
<br><br>Now that Cassie is officially in 'The Club' and now known as one of the 'in' group at school she finds life so much better, she feels welcome and wanted, not like a disease everyone is trying to avoid. Unfortunately for her she is dealing with her desires for Adam, Diana's boyfriend, whom she fell in love with on the beach last summer (One meeting is all it took...). She loves Diana and she would never want to do anything to hurt her so she avoids Adam at all costs.<br><br>Meanwhile, the coven are still dealing with the crystal skull and the dark magic that was released from it the first time they tried to activate it. People keep dying and they have no idea why or what the connection is so they're trying to do everything they can to figure out this mess.
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374832i/729128.png" alt="" width="315" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br>In this book Cassie was a lot stronger than she was in the first book. You see her grow and change. That's nice to see because I know that if she hadn't of grown I would have gotten tired of her and the way she always needed to lean on people for support. You see her take control of herself in this book.<br><br>Diana is still as strong and as lovely as ever. Although she is seen as a bit too naïve in this book, too trusting but she has no reason not to trust anyone. So I feel it's completely justified and that she's not naïve she just completely and wholly trusts the people she's close to. As you should.<br><br>Adam is strong and someone you could trust. He puts people before himself. I love that, he's definitely the one to call if you need help. In this book we get to see way more of him, he's a good guy yet also comes across as kind of mysterious.<br><br>Nick is mysterious but temperamental. Still he grows in this book and becomes a little more patient and interested in the coven. He's so mysterious that I've developed a little crush on him and I really want something to happen between him and Cassie! What is it about guys that are mysterious? I guess it's because they just don't tell <em>anyone</em> what they're thinking or feeling you kind of have the fight for it so it's not easy, or something like that.<br><br>Faye is as bitchy and nasty as ever. Yet I still don't hate her, you can see that she has this nice side to her. You can even see why she does the things she does to get what she wants. They're completely selfish reasons but those reasons always have to do with herself, they're never just so she makes people feel horrible. That's a by-product of her actions...<br><br>We get to see a bit more of everyone else in the coven without getting lost at who's who, I think that's very important because when there's so many characters in a book if they're not described well or there isn't a subtle hint at who they are you get lost very easily and can't remember who's who and who is what to each other. That didn't happen in this book. I found everything to be clear.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375548i/730149.png" alt="" width="315" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Personally I really liked this book too. I think it was as good as the first one in every way. There was some thing about the writing of this book that just drew me in, in every moment I was asking questions or trying to find out the answers to questions I had already asked. Who was this person? What did this mean? I was trying to put the pieces together to figure out what was going on but some of the clues were so subtle that by the end of the book I was still surprised. I love it when you haven't guessed the reveal at all in a book even though those clues and hints are there.<br><br>I haven't read all of L. J. Smith's books but I am really enjoying this series so I think I will check out her other books as well.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374832i/729131.png" alt="" width="315" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I think this book was entertaining, a fun read and a book that I could come home to and just relax with. There wasn't anything that I found hard to read, I wasn't disgusted or confused by anything I was just a little shocked. A little shock is always good.<br><br>I was pretty interested in the content too, like all the little witchery stuff, the crystals they used for certain things, the herbs they used for certain things. I kind of wish I had had an aunt or something that was interested in that stuff and had taught me all about it as I grew up. And by 'stuff' I mean the good uses for crystals and herbs etc .<br><br>I really liked this book, just as much as the first one so I'm pretty excited to read the next book to see what happens!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374832i/729130.png" alt="" width="315" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was written in 1992.<br><br>As I was reading this book it definitely gave off this vibe of the 90's. Like the way people thought, the fact no one had cell phones at school or at all. You had to call someone from an actual phone that was plugged in to the wall, if you were by yourself and realised you were in danger you were pretty much screwed since you couldn't just txt someone. So that's not good but it was true. <br><br>It felt like life was less cluttered with technology and everyone was closer and communicated better because you <em>had</em> to go over to someone's house to see them, you <em>had</em> to call someone on the phone to talk to them you couldn't just txt them, you had to make the effort. I never call people these days to talk to them, but I think I will start. I kind of miss that communication. <br><br>I also got the impression that the kids/teenagers treated their elders with respect, more respect than I see a lot of kids/teenagers do these days. That's a sad thought to think that I don't know of many young people that use manners profusely or respect their elders. Perhaps that's just the area I live in, or perhaps that's just what I choose to see. Now I'm just rambling.<br><br>As I envisioned everything it reminded me of the 90's and my childhood. The excitement of the outdoors, or sleep overs with friends where we would get up to mischief like midnight snacks or talk about our crushes the whole night, there was no bitching about anyone and there was no spending hours and hours on the computer... I was only 2 in 1992 so I guess I'm thinking more of 1998 but still, it was this weird nostalgic feeling that I got.<br><br>Life these days doesn't feel anything like it did back then. Maybe that's because I was a kid and saw life through a different set of eyes. Obviously I see it differently now but it's just interesting to remember how much this world has changed from twenty years a go.<br><br>Also, the male protagonists in this book compared to the YA books now are <em>so</em> different. Well that's how I feel. They aren't treating the girls like crap, deliberately hurting them or ignoring them, they aren't masking their feelings for them, they're honest and straight forward about it. And I bet if they did the girls wouldn't take it, they would stand up for themselves. Maybe that's only in this book but it all feels less complicated. Where has chivalry gone?! I sound like I'm really old now...<br><br>Miss J<br> x </span>
  <a data-text-id="2916708401617635628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9946595307270579625" style="display:none">This is book 2 in The Secret Circle series. See my review of book 1 here. This book was just as good as the first in the series. The tension is building as Cassie is black mailed into helping Faye wrestle power away from Diana. Cassie finds herself hurting those she cares most about and also suffers a great loss in her family. <div id="review_751134417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751134417" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7549226-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440281456p2/7549226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/751134417?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/7549226-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">witch lovers like myself</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=saw-the-movie-or-tv-show">saw-the-movie-or-tv-show</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7549226-cindy?shelf=lj-smith">lj-smith</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer751134417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer293036389310286931">Cassie is being blackmailed by Faye. But doing what Faye asks will be the ultimate form of betrayal. Will Cassie go through with it?<br/>If she doesn't, she runs the risk of destroying her relationship with Diana, and perhaps the entire Circle. But if she does, something evil might be unleashed on New Salem. An old and very powerful evil.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>In my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/879215.The_Initiation__The_Secret_Circle___1_' title='The Initiation (The Secret Circle, #1) by L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Initiation</a>, I mentioned I'm biased on this trilogy. Biased as hell. Wish I wasn't, but I am.<br/><br/>For one thing, I was obsessed with the TV show. I als</span>
  <span id="freeText293036389310286931" style="display:none">Cassie is being blackmailed by Faye. But doing what Faye asks will be the ultimate form of betrayal. Will Cassie go through with it?<br />If she doesn't, she runs the risk of destroying her relationship with Diana, and perhaps the entire Circle. But if she does, something evil might be unleashed on New Salem. An old and very powerful evil.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />In my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/879215.The_Initiation__The_Secret_Circle___1_" title="The Initiation (The Secret Circle, #1) by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Initiation</a>, I mentioned I'm biased on this trilogy. Biased as hell. Wish I wasn't, but I am.<br /><br />For one thing, I was obsessed with the TV show. I also happen to love just abut all of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/50873.L_J__Smith" title="L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">L.J. Smith</a>'s books. Most of all, though, I love love love witches. I don't care if they're green and fly around on brooms like the Wicked Witch of the West. I don't care if they use wands and are incredibly smart like Hermione. I don't care if they are blonde and own a talking cat like Sabrina the Teenage Witch. And I don't care if they're young, beautiful, selfish, and headed for destruction like the witches in The Secret Circle trilogy. <br /><br />I was not expecting to like this book as much as I did. Most people that rate this book 4-5 stars read it during their teenage years and rate it so high because it brings back nostalgia.<br />They read it as teenagers, some even pre-teens and just loved it. Some even went ahead and re-read it now as adults and found it to be simple and childish. That's understandable.<br /><br />The thing is, I read this just today. I'm in my 20s and I am rating this 5 stars. I'll even go ahead and say that I would give it 5 stars even if I wasn't biased. Why? Because this book is awesome. It is. The ending was so exciting to me and I'm glad there is still one remaining book in this series for me to read.<br /><br /><br />I am not exaggerating when I say this book blew me away. It has now become one of my favorite books OF ALL TIME.<br />It's short and, yes I'll admit it, pretty simple. I read it in a matter of hours and the further I got into the story, the more invested I became.<br /><br />But it had it's flaws. It really did. But damn it if I didn't find the flaws absolutely hilarious.<br />I <b>loved</b> the fact that three people were murdered in or near the school but it is never really investigated. The police show up, don't find any clues and that's that. They don't conduct investigations, there are no suspects, no arrests, nothing. The school doesn't even get shut down or anything.<br />I can't express to you how hilarious this is to me. Even thinking about it now makes me laugh.<br />The funny thing is, had this happened in any other book, any other series, I would've undoubtedly bitched about it to the end of the world and back.<br /><br />The apathy of the characters really shines through when another student dies and one of the girls says “What about the Halloween dance?” …<br />“Guys, another person at our school just died and that's sad and all, but I don't want to miss the dance. I already bought the perfect shoes and everything!” Okay, so that last part isn't an exact quote, but you get it.<br /><br />Cassie makes some really stupid decisions. Like when she goes to the cemetery in the middle of the night. Even though just a few hours earlier they saw a mysterious and possibly dangerous ghost lurking around. Girl....<br /><br />Like I said, these things didn't bother me at all. I relished in this book's flaws. I love it more BECAUSE of it's flaws.<br /><br /><br />The main character of this book, Cassie, did a 180 attitude wise. Last book she was naïve and grateful for the kindness people showed her, and shy.<br />In this book she's mean. She's jumpy and catty and easily ticked off and... more daring, I guess.<br /><br />What really surprised me , though, was the fact that halfway through the book I realized I actually liked Faye. Which is bizarre. Faye is a bitch. Faye is annoying. Faye always ends a sentence with a “throaty chuckle” or some weird kind of laugh that I can't remember how to describe. It's annoying as fuck. But I like her. Underneath all that wickedness, oozing sexuality, and beauty is a sad, sad lady. Maybe she's sad because her mom is always sick and unavailable to her. I don't know. I just want to say: I see through you, Faye Chamberlain. All you really need is a hug and someone to be there for you. I'm not saying I want to be the one to hug you or be there for you, I'm just saying, you need someone to love you unconditionally. Go out and find yourself someone nice to love.<br /><br /><br />This book also helped me realize that I am falling for Nick. And for no good reason, either. He's still a godforsaken enigma. I don't know anything about him. Other than he's a tall, sullen, brooding, quiet, indifferent, alcohol drinking, cigarette smoking, handsome devil. And that there's a slight chance he miiiiight like Cassie.<br />And now I want them to end up together, dammit!<br />I mean, yeah, I like Adam but he's just so... good. Which translates to boring.<br />I need adventure and a tiny little bit of romance and unpredictability. I mean, <b>Cassie</b> needs adventure and a tiny little bit of romance and unpredictability. Hehe.<br /><br />Hear my plea, oh great L.J. Smith! Allow Cassie and Nick to be together forever!<br /><br />The Captive is now a favorite of mine. I don't care how stupid or childish it seems. I love it. I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/395921.The_Power__The_Secret_Circle___3_" title="The Power (The Secret Circle, #3) by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Power</a>!<br /><br />Quotes:<br /><i>”I don't know what's going on, and it's none of my business, anyway. But I'd like to go to the dance with you.” -pg. 195<br /><br />“It's yours, Cassie. From my grandmother to me to you. You have the sight and the power, as I did, as your mother does. But you can't run away like she did. You have to stay here and face him.”<br /><br />“Never be afraid, Cassie. There's nothing frightening in the dark if you just face it.” -pg. 292</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="293036389310286931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText2598306452122826520" style="display:none">THIS is a guilty pleasure, if ever there was one!<br /><br />Rereading this series now, last time (2011-2012-ish) I didn’t make it through all the books, according to my bookmark I only made it about 4.5 chapters into THE POWER before I gave up. <br />This time around the tv-show isn’t as fresh in my head and I’m not struggling to keep them apart (they are SO different, I remember just being confused by the books last time). <br />TSC really is a 90s/soap opera/ teenage/ drama/witchy mashup thingy...which doesn’t mean that it’s particularly GOOD, but rather pretty bad... but entertaining in a nostalgic kinda way. Like a good old 90s pop song (you’ll sing and dance your ass off if it comes on but you’d NEVER listen to it at home). Well, this is what this series is to me. Let’s hope I’ll make it through the last book this time around. <br /><br />And again: fuck you, Adam. I hate girls fighting over some looser guy, blaming and hating on each other while NO ONE HOLDS THE DUDE ACCOUNTABLE. Ugh. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_125280245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125280245" />
    <a title="♥Xeni♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3584794-xeni"><img alt="♥Xeni♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338844476p2/3584794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125280245?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Xeni♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Xeni♥" href="/user/show/3584794-xeni">♥Xeni♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=2012-books-read">2012-books-read</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125280245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8041639212070417358">Woot, just reread this! My main point? I wish that they had taken the last scene (actually, all of it) and at least stuck that one into the tv show. Eerie red lights and weird shadow figures killing grandma's? Freaky as shit! Instead, we get parents murdering their parents. Yeah, that might be more 'realistic' in a witch drama show. Maybe. Actually, a demon/devil/spirit dude killing for revenge is a lot more likely of a scenario.<br/><br/>Completely easy to read by now, but it's still a good book. This on</span>
  <span id="freeText8041639212070417358" style="display:none">Woot, just reread this! My main point? I wish that they had taken the last scene (actually, all of it) and at least stuck that one into the tv show. Eerie red lights and weird shadow figures killing grandma's? Freaky as shit! Instead, we get parents murdering their parents. Yeah, that might be more 'realistic' in a witch drama show. Maybe. Actually, a demon/devil/spirit dude killing for revenge is a lot more likely of a scenario.<br /><br />Completely easy to read by now, but it's still a good book. This one is completely wretched in that Cassie get's blackmailed pretty much into a realm of psychological torture by Faye (who, lets face it, is a lot scarier in the book than she is in the TV show). Every time I read through the 'reveal' scene, I get chills. Probably because the first time I read this series I pretty heavily identified with Cassie and it all just felt so real. These days, I really do wish that the writing was more up to my level, but hey, you read a YA book, you read a YA book. <br /><br />Now, on to book three!</span>

<div id="review_2966650232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2966650232" />
    <a title="Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48121966-autumn"><img alt="Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448854774p2/48121966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2966650232?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Autumn" href="/user/show/48121966-autumn">Autumn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062125446" href="/book/show/13425499-secret-circle-vol-ii">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48121966-autumn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48121966-autumn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48121966-autumn?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48121966-autumn?shelf=quarantine">quarantine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966650232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17799754585912797299">If there's one thing about <i>The Secret Circle</i> that amazes me, it's that this series wasn't bigger.<br/><br/>Part of it, I'm sure, was just a matter of timing. The original trilogy was published in the early-90s, before YA was considered a legitimate genre and filmmakers realized that they could make billions by marketing movies to teenagers (there was, of course, a TV adaptation of this series, but it largely flew under the radar and was cancelled after only one season). The format is a little unusual--the</span>
  <span id="freeText17799754585912797299" style="display:none">If there's one thing about <i>The Secret Circle</i> that amazes me, it's that this series wasn't bigger.<br /><br />Part of it, I'm sure, was just a matter of timing. The original trilogy was published in the early-90s, before YA was considered a legitimate genre and filmmakers realized that they could make billions by marketing movies to teenagers (there was, of course, a TV adaptation of this series, but it largely flew under the radar and was cancelled after only one season). The format is a little unusual--the series is essentially one long story broken into three sections, with each book ending in an awkward place and picking up in the same spot in the next book. Nevertheless, the story is fun and well-paced, with interesting mythology and enjoyable characters (even if they aren't always realistic). <br /><br />I've read a lot of YA in my day (although not nearly as much as other people on Goodreads), and do believe that L.J. Smith is a better writer than at least two-thirds of the ones writing today. This is largely based on her ability to take a circle of twelve characters and make them each feel distinct from one another. Some characters are maybe a little too strongly archetypal (namely Diana the angel and Faye the devil), but even then they're still fun to read about. There's something nice about the small, seemingly unimportant scenes that Smith includes of the girls just hanging out and revealing their interests. Cassie's friends, Melanie and Laurel, take a back seat in this installment, but we do see more of Faye's wingwomen, Deborah and Suzan, who are slowly beginning to accept Cassie, even if they still don't consider her a friend. If anything, because the other girls have such dynamic personalities, Cassie often pales in comparison, taking on the passive self-insert role that readers have come to dread.<br /><br /><i>The Captive</i> isn't as unintentionally lesbian as <i>The Initiation</i>, but it's still there. (On a side note, Deborah is consistently shown to not be interested in men in a way that suggests she is asexual, which is pleasantly refreshing to read, but I can't help but wonder if maybe <i>she</i> was the character who was supposed to be gay-coded after all). This is strengthened by what is probably the weakest part of the series: the main romance. Two books in and Adam is still fairly two-dimensional, as is his apparently star-crossed love story with Cassie. The two of them hardly know each other and barely interact, yet their relationship is supposed to be the driving force of <i>The Captive</i>. <br /><br />As other reviews have mentioned, this book will pique your interest in more enigmatic characters like Nick, who are sadly not given as much focus as the main trifecta of Cassie-Diana-Faye. Despite all the controversy around the second <i>Secret Circle</i> trilogy (check out those Goodreads pages to see what I'm talking about), I'm hoping that the additional books will mean that we'll be able to learn more about the rest of the Circle. <br /><br />There's a pretty big exposition-dump towards the end of the book, but it's spooky and weird enough to be forgiven. I'm looking forward to finding out what happens next. And now, on to Part 3!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17799754585912797299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5240129813566313701">I watched the cancelled series "The Secret Circle", but the books are nothing like that. The first, "Initiation", was okay, a fast read, sometimes intriguing. I love stories about witches. But this one is awful. The plot is incomprehensible and incredibly slow.   <span id="freeText5240129813566313701" style="display:none">I watched the cancelled series "The Secret Circle", but the books are nothing like that. The first, "Initiation", was okay, a fast read, sometimes intriguing. I love stories about witches. But this one is awful. The plot is incomprehensible and incredibly slow. Most of the time the witches just dress up and go out dancing. Sometimes they seduce pizza boys for fun. Yes, the pizza boys are mainly young and beautiful, like almost everyone in this book. It's a pity they don't have the hair like "moonlight and sunlight woven together" like Diana though. The main story is stupid and totally random. The members of the Circle were searching for some artifact for a long time, Adam brought it home, it was supposed to amplify their powers or something? And then it suddenly becomes the worst thing in the world and kills people. A surprise twist! Cassie gets pushed around by Faye (the only character I found slightly interesting) and then she decides to stand up for herself, hell, because her dying grandmother said she is the most powerful witch of them all. I actually stopped caring halfway.</span>

  <span id="freeText15079825842348163579" style="display:none">Secret Circle: The Captive, was definitely better than The Initiation. I however was not impressed by the forbidden love between Adam and Cassie, the way in which is written is not believable even if its based on the whole soulmate principle, not enough happens between the Adam and Cassie for her to fall for him, so easily and quickly... I also think that Nick should have held a bigger role in the love story, his character is so mysterious and intriguing, I personally think he would of been a better choice of soulmate for Cassie and would have made for a better, more interesting and intriguing love story. </span>

  <span id="freeText1287623438906105856" style="display:none">I don't usually write harsh reviews and I really tried to give this series a chance. The first book failed to keep my interest but I gave the second book a shot, thinking okay maybe the author is just getting started. The first book was very slow, almost like an introduction to the story. However this book failed to go anywhere as well. Every book is supposed to have a setting, problem, rising action, climax, falling action and the ending. The problem in this book, which I will not mention to avoid spoilers, was not Interesting enough to carry the plot, which lead to there being a poor climax. In addition, the characters are not relatable and not very interesting, which is maybe why the problem was not Interesting to me. I was unable to sympathize with any of the characters. The only thing that made the book even slightly interesting is Faye. Even though she's supposed to be evil and basically the antagonist, I keep hoping she'll do something bad just to have something interesting to read about. I'm not finished reading the book but I'm not sure that I will.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nn2XCaGbgRHNkRlMa4JY4UTbI/ZHh2QCvGbgp6hYWZcRe0FQebXSsOTZAy0BUtJSVpGqulLnRoX+z/bDKlwTQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('17sUcB71GloozC8hi81RsoEFLQdP9Gd08tRelwTtPg9YvcIpxttJ+wGENUDhHdsBk0+kS1qURfOwfUjzhul02A==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer3394575626130216724">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series'>https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br/><br/><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in th</span>
  <span id="freeText3394575626130216724" style="display:none">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series">https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br /><br /><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in the Bay Area of California, with a backyard that is full of flowers, which she adores, especially with many different shades of roses.<br /><br />She loves to visit a friend's little cabin in the Point Reyes National Seashore area, which has lots of trees, lots of animals, lots of beaches to walk on, and lots of places to hike. Once, while hiking, she saw a snow-white buck which allowed her to follow it nearly half a mile. She also likes to collect things: angels (they remind her of her late mother), tiny boxes from different countries or of fanciful shape, nineteenth century children's literature, and books about quantum physics--especially about the mystery of the dark energy in the universe. A militant optimist, she is also part of the Velociraptor Sisterhood (a fancy way of saying that she likes to read, write and discuss books with strong female characters), and she has traveled extensively in Europe and the Far East. The two countries she loves to visit most are Great Britain, with its historic monuments and amazing country landscapes, and Japan, with its bustling urban life and exquisite mountain scenery.<br /><br />Her favorite current writer is Terry Pratchett, the author of the Discworld series, for its wild and witty satires on life, death, war, love, assassins, coppers, and Australia. Her favorite classical writer is Jane Austen. Her favorite poets are Robert Frost and Emily Dickinson. Her favorite movies are The Seven Samurai and Avatar (analyze that!). She doesn't have a favorite TV show, because she doesn't have time to watch TV (and only owns one for playing movies).<br /><br />Her favorite people are her readers, each of whom she cherishes with deep and lasting affection.<br /><br /><i>Note: L. J. Smith wrote books 1-7 of The Vampire Diaries series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. wrote books 1-3 of The Secret Circle series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. did not write any of the Originals or Stefan's Diaries. These were written by Kevin Williamson and/or various ghostwritters.</i> <br /></span>
